✠
Encyclical Letter · 教宗通諭

MAGNIFICA HUMANITAS

「壯麗的人性」通諭

Encyclical Letter of His Holiness Pope Leo XIV on Safeguarding the Human Person in the Time of Artificial Intelligence

教宗良十四世論「在人工智能時代守護人性尊嚴」通諭

His Holiness Pope Leo XIV教宗良十四世
Vatican, 15 May 2026 · 梵蒂岡，二○二六年五月十五日

INTRODUCTION · 引言
· · ·
¶ 1
Humanity, created by God in all its grandeur, is today facing a pivotal choice: either to construct a new Tower of Babel or to build the city in which God and humanity dwell together. Each generation inherits the task of shaping its own era, of guiding history to become a place where the dignity of every person is safeguarded, justice is promoted and fraternity is made possible. Yet every era also runs the risk of creating an inhumane and more unjust world. Whenever humanity is in danger of marring its true identity, we Christians lift our eyes to the Incarnate God, knowing that it is “only in the mystery of the Word made flesh that the mystery of humanity truly becomes clear.” [1] In Jesus Christ, this humanity in its grandeur becomes the Way, the Truth and the Life, opening the path for each of us to grow toward fullness.
¶ 1
天主在祂的全部壯麗中所創造的人類，今日正面臨一個關鍵的抉擇：是要興建一座新的「巴貝耳塔」，還是要建設一座天主與人共居的城。每一代都承繼着塑造自己時代的使命，引導歷史成為一個守護每個人的尊嚴、推動正義、實現兄弟情誼的場所。然而，每一個時代亦同樣面對危機，可能造就一個非人性、更為不義的世界。每當人性有失其真實身分的危險之際，我們基督徒便舉目仰望那降生成人的天主，深知「唯獨在那聖言成了血肉的奧蹟中，人類的奧蹟才真正得以彰顯」[1]。在耶穌基督內，這壯麗的人性成了道路、真理和生命，為我們每一個人開闢一條走向圓滿成全的道路。
¶ 2
Founded on Christ, the living stone, we experience the powerful and mysterious action of the Holy Spirit, and we believe that every authentic human effort to cooperate with him for the good will be blessed by our heavenly Father, in whom we place our hope. For this reason, we can diligently contribute to every initiative that builds a more just world, and we can call others to collaborate in promoting the integral development of every human being. We wish to engage in dialogue with all men and women of our time, with whom we share in the events, questions and aspirations of humanity. [2] Together with them, we seek to identify new paths for the common good and for promoting a dignified life for all. Indeed, openness to dialogue is an integral part of the Church’s vocation because, constituted in Christ as “a sacrament… of communion with God and of the unity of the entire human race,” [3] she recognizes history as the place where the Gospel challenges and directs human experience.
¶ 2
我們以基督，那「活石」，為根基，體驗到聖神大能而奧妙的工作；我們深信，凡為善而與祂同工的一切真誠的人性努力，必蒙我們在天大父賜福——我們的希望，正寄於祂內。為此，我們可以不懈地為一切建設更公義世界的計劃作出貢獻，並可以呼籲他人共同推動每一個人的全人發展。我們願與當代所有的男女展開對話——我們與他們同處於人類的各種事件、提問與盼望之中[2]。我們同他們一起，尋求新的途徑，以促進公益和維護人人的尊嚴生活。誠然，對話的開放是教會聖召不可分割的一部分，因為教會在基督內被立為「與天主共融、並使全人類合一的聖事」[3]，故視歷史為福音向人類經驗發出挑戰並指引方向的場所。
¶ 3
In this spirit, Pope Leo XIII published his Encyclical Rerum Novarum in 1891, the 135 th anniversary of which we celebrate with deep gratitude this year. With that document, my beloved predecessor gave impetus to the reflection on society, the economy and politics, which is now known as the “Social Doctrine of the Church.” When some objected that the Church should not waste energy on worldly matters, but instead focus on communicating the message of eternal life, Leo XIII responded with realism and wisdom, saying that the proclamation of the Gospel cannot overlook the concrete lives of people. [4] Many decades have passed since then, and the Magisterium, pastors, theologians and faithful have continued to reflect on social issues in the light of the Gospel. Today, the Social Doctrine of the Church is a legacy of wisdom, where we find principles for thought, criteria for discernment and judgment, and concrete guidelines for action. Founded on Sacred Scripture and Tradition, and in engagement with the sciences, it helps us clearly interpret the challenges of the present and identify appropriate ways for living out a clear Christian witness, with joy and in service to the world. It is not an inert set of concepts, but a living corpus of truth that safeguards and interprets humanity’s vocation to a full and just life. I therefore wish to add my own voice to this living tradition, invoking the help of the Spirit of wisdom, who has dwelt in the world since its beginning (cf. Prov 8:22-31).
¶ 3
本着這份精神，教宗良十三世於一八九一年頒布了《新事》通諭——今年，我們以深切的感恩之心慶祝該通諭頒布一百三十五週年。藉着這份文獻，我這位敬愛的前任教宗推動了對社會、經濟與政治的反省，今日被稱為「教會社會訓導」。當時有人反對說，教會不應浪費精力於塵世事務，而應專注於宣講永生的訊息；對此良十三世以實事求是的智慧回應：宣講福音不能忽視人民的具體生活[4]。多少年代過去了，歷代訓導、牧者、神學家和信眾，繼續在福音的光照下省思社會問題。今日，教會社會訓導已成為一份智慧的傳承：我們在其中找到思考的原則、辨明與判斷的準則，以及行動的具體方針。它以聖經和聖傳為根基，並與各門科學對話，幫助我們清晰地解讀當代的挑戰，並指出與之相應的方式，去喜樂地、為服務世界而活出明確的基督徒見證。它並不是一套僵死的概念，而是一個有生命的真理體系，守護並闡釋人類獲享圓滿而正義生活的召叫。為此，我願將自己的聲音加入這個活的傳統，懇求那智慧之神的協助——祂自世界肇始以來，已居於世間（參箴 8:22-31）。
The res novae of our time
我們這時代的「新事」
¶ 4
While Leo XIII spoke in his time of “new things” ( rerum novarum), today we cannot limit ourselves simply to repeating his insightful teachings. Instead, we must ask God for the wisdom to interpret the great trends of our time, particularly technological advances. In recent years, it has become increasingly evident how rapidly and profoundly digitalization, artificial intelligence (AI) and robotics are transforming our world. Technology should not be considered, in itself, as a force antagonistic to humanity. On the contrary, it has formed part of our history since the beginning as “a profoundly human reality, linked to the autonomy and freedom of man.” [5] Over the centuries, technological development has significantly improved the living conditions of humanity. At the same time, each phase of progress has also revealed the ambiguity of tools that can cause harm when not oriented toward the good. Today, however, we find ourselves facing a new situation. The power and prevalence of emerging technologies are interwoven into the fabric of daily life, shaping decision-making processes and deeply affecting the collective imagination: “Never has humanity had such power over itself.” [6] New technologies open up a horizon extending in directions that are imaginable but not yet fully predictable. This complicates the assessment of their potential impact and the long-term effects they may have on both the dignity of individuals and the common good.
¶ 4
雖然良十三世在他的時代曾論及「新事」（rerum novarum），但我們今天不能僅僅滿足於重述他富有洞見的訓導。相反，我們必須祈求天主賜下智慧，俾能解讀我們這時代的重大趨勢，尤其是科技的進展。近年來，數碼化、人工智能（AI）和機械人技術，正以何等迅速而深刻的方式轉變我們的世界，已愈來愈顯而易見。科技本身不應被視為與人性對立的力量。相反，科技自人類歷史之初便是其一部分，是「一個與人的自主和自由密切相連的、深具人性的事實」[5]。多個世紀以來，科技的發展顯著改善了人類的生活條件。同時，每一階段的進步，也揭示了工具本身的雙重性——一旦不導向善，便能造成傷害。然而今日，我們發現自己面對一個新的處境。新興科技的力量與普遍性，已交織於日常生活的肌理之中，塑造着決策的過程，並深刻影響着集體的想像：「人類從未對自身擁有過如此巨大的力量」[6]。新科技打開的視域，雖可想像，卻尚未能完全預測。這使得評估其潛在影響和長期效應，無論對個人的尊嚴抑或公益，都變得錯綜複雜。
¶ 5
It now falls to us to face the challenges of our time with clarity of thought and responsibility. It is necessary to establish adequate regulatory tools capable of upholding justice and curbing the distorting effects of technological power. Nevertheless, the issue is not limited to regulation. As Pope Francis warned, we must realistically ask ourselves who holds this power today and how they use it: “It must also be recognized that nuclear energy, biotechnology, information technology, knowledge of our own DNA, and many other abilities which we have acquired… have given those with the knowledge, and especially the economic resources to use them, an impressive dominance over the whole of humanity and the entire world.” [7] In the past, it was largely up to the State to guide and direct innovation. Today, however, the main drivers of development are private, often transnational, parties that are endowed with resources and the capacity to intervene that surpass those of many Governments. Technological power thus takes on an unprecedented, predominantly “private” aspect, which makes it even more challenging to discern, govern and direct such power toward the common good.
¶ 5
如今擺在我們眼前的，是以清晰的思想和負責任的態度面對當代的挑戰。我們必須建立適當的監管工具，以維護正義並遏制科技力量所帶來的扭曲效應。然而，問題不能僅限於監管。正如教宗方濟各曾警告的，我們必須切實地問自己：今日的這份力量掌握在誰的手中？又是如何被使用？「我們亦必須承認，核能、生物科技、資訊科技、對人類自身 DNA 的認識，以及我們所取得的許多其他能力……已使那些擁有知識的人，特別是擁有經濟資源運用這些能力的人，對整個人類和整個世界享有令人驚嘆的支配。」[7] 在過往，引導和指揮創新的角色大致由國家承擔；而今天，發展的主要推動者卻是私人——通常是跨國的——團體，他們所擁有的資源和介入能力，已超越許多政府。因此，科技力量呈現出前所未有的、以「私人」性質為主的面貌，這使得辨明、管治和將其導向公益的工作更加困難。
¶ 6
For this reason it is necessary to begin a shared discernment process for identifying the spiritual and cultural roots of ongoing transformations. If we focus only on contingencies, we risk letting the succession of emergencies dictate the direction of our path. We are living through a rapid phase of transition, a “change of era,” in which — while some are vying for the future of new technologies and others dedicate themselves to reflecting on the matter — most people are watching and waiting, observing from afar and merely hoping for the best. For this very reason, crucial questions impose themselves on our conscience and can no longer be avoided: Where are we going? Toward what goal do we wish to orient ourselves? What direction should we choose as a people and as a human community?
¶ 6
為此，我們必須開展一個共同的辨明過程，以識別現今這場轉化在精神和文化上的根源。如果我們只專注於眼前的偶然事件，便冒險讓接踵而至的「緊急情況」決定我們的路向。我們正處於一個迅速過渡的階段，一個「時代的轉變」：在這當中，有人爭奪新科技的未來，有人致力於對此進行反省，而大多數人卻只是在觀望、等待，從遠處旁觀，僅僅希望事情能往好的方向發展。正因如此，那些攸關性的問題已加諸我們的良知之上，再不能迴避：我們要往哪裏去？我們希望將自己引向甚麼目標？作為一個民族、作為人類的群體，我們應選擇怎樣的方向？
Two biblical images
兩幅聖經圖像
¶ 7
In order to answer these questions and discern how to navigate responsibly the era of AI, I would like to bring to mind two scenes from the Bible: the construction of the Tower of Babel (cf. Gen 11:1-9) and the rebuilding of the walls of Jerusalem (cf. Neh 2–6). The story of Babel appears in the Book of Genesis, at the origins of humanity, immediately after the genealogies of Noah’s sons. After settling in a plain in the land of Shinar, the people decided to build a city and a tower “with its top in the heavens” (Gen 11:4). Fearing being scattered across the earth, they sought to guarantee stability and power for themselves, and above all to “make a name” for themselves. It was an impressive feat: a single language, a single technology, a single direction. However, the project concealed a profound danger. It was a project conceived without reference to God, supported by a uniformity that eliminated diversity and that chose homogenization over communion. When a city is built on pride and the claim to self-sufficiency, communication breaks down, languages are confused and people no longer understand each other. The result is not unity, but dispersion. Babel thus reveals the limits of any effort that, however grandiose, arises from self-affirmation, sacrifices human dignity for efficiency and aspires to reach heaven without God’s blessing.
¶ 7
為了回應這些問題，並辨明在人工智能時代如何負責任地航行，我願喚起聖經中兩個場景：建造巴貝耳塔的故事（參創 11:1-9）和重建耶路撒冷城牆的故事（參厄下 2-6）。巴貝耳的故事，出現在《創世紀》中，置於人類的起源，緊接諾厄諸子的族譜之後。當人們在史納爾地的平原定居後，便決定建造一座城和一座「塔頂摩天」的塔（創 11:4）。他們害怕分散到全地面上，便謀求為自己保證安定和力量，並尤其想為自己「立名」。這是一項令人印象深刻的事業：一種語言、一種科技、一個方向。然而，這個計劃隱藏着深刻的危險。它是一個沒有顧及天主的計劃，建基於一種抹殺差異的劃一性之上，以同質取代了共融。當一座城建在驕傲與自足的主張之上時，溝通便會崩潰，語言便會混亂，人與人便不再彼此理解。其結果並非合一，而是分散。巴貝耳由此揭示了一切自我中心的努力——無論多麼宏偉——的界限：以效率犧牲人的尊嚴，妄圖不憑天主的祝福而直達天庭。
¶ 8
The Book of Nehemiah, in turn, opens at a time of great vulnerability in the history of ancient Israel. After the Babylonian exile, a portion of the people returned to Jerusalem, but the city was still in ruins, the walls collapsed and the gates burned (cf. Neh 1–2). Nehemiah, a Jew in the service of the Persian King Artaxerxes, received news of the disastrous state of his ancestral city. Before taking action, he fasted, prayed and interceded for the people. He then asked the king for permission to return to Jerusalem and, upon arriving, examined the destroyed areas in silence. He did not impose solutions from above. He convened the families, assigned each of them a section of the wall to rebuild, listened to their concerns, coordinated their efforts and addressed any opposition. The narrative shows how the city is reborn, not through the initiative of one man, but through the shared responsibility of all: men, women, priests, artisans, heads of households and young people all play a part. It is an undertaking with God at the center, which rebuilds relationships before rebuilding with stones. Thus, ancient Jerusalem rediscovers a common language — not one of uniformity, but one of communion, namely the harmony that arises when all persons assume their own role and recognize that their strength comes from the Lord.
¶ 8
《厄斯德拉下》一卷則於古代以色列歷史中一個極為脆弱的時刻開卷。經歷了巴比倫流亡之後，一部分子民返回耶路撒冷，但城仍是廢墟：城牆倒塌，城門被火燒毀（參厄下 1-2）。乃赫米雅，這位事奉波斯王阿塔薛西斯的猶太人，得到祖城淒慘景況的消息。在採取行動之前，他禁食、祈禱、為人民代禱。其後，他求王准許自己返回耶路撒冷；抵達後，他靜默地視察了被毀的地方。他並沒有自上而下強加方案，而是召集各家庭，分派他們每家一段城牆來重建，傾聽他們的憂慮，協調他們的努力，並處理一切反對的聲音。敘述中可見：這座城的重生，不是憑藉一個人的倡議，而是憑藉眾人共同的責任——男人、女人、司祭、工匠、家長和年輕人——人人都有自己的角色。這是一項以天主為中心的事業：先重建關係，然後才以石頭重建。如此，古耶路撒冷重新尋回一種共同的語言——並非劃一的語言，而是共融的語言：當每一個人承擔起自己的角色，並承認自己的力量來自上主時，所自然湧現的那份和諧。
¶ 9
In light of these two images, the Holy Spirit challenges us today regarding our relationship with technology and the ongoing digital revolution. Scientific discoveries are talents entrusted to humanity so that they may bear fruit (cf. Mt 25:14-30). Technology has the power to heal, connect, educate and protect our common home; but it can also divide, exclude and generate new forms of injustice. In the abstract, technology in and of itself is not a solution to humanity’s problems, just as it is not inherently evil. In practice, however, technology is never neutral, because it takes on the characteristics of those who devise, finance, regulate and use it. Therefore, the primary choice is not between a “yes” or “no” to technology, but rather between constructing Babel or rebuilding Jerusalem; between a power that claims to dominate the heavens and a people who work together in the presence of God to rebuild the walls of fraternal coexistence.
¶ 9
在這兩幅圖像的光照下，聖神今日就我們與科技的關係，以及這場正在進行的數碼革命，向我們發出挑戰。科學的發現是託付給人類的「塔冷通」，為使它們結出果實（參瑪 25:14-30）。科技有能力醫治、聯繫、教育和保護我們的共同家園；但它也能分裂、排斥，並催生新形式的不義。在抽象層面上，科技本身既不是人類問題的答案，也不是本質上邪惡的；但實際上，科技從來不是中立的，因為它承載着那些設計、資助、規範和使用者的特質。因此，根本的選擇並不在於對科技說「是」還是「否」，而在於：是要建造巴貝耳，還是要重建耶路撒冷？是要那妄圖支配諸天的力量，還是那共同在天主面前同工、重建兄弟共處之牆的子民？
¶ 10
We must, then, avoid the “Babel syndrome,” namely the idolatry of profit that sacrifices the weak, a uniformity that neutralizes differences, and the pretense that a single language — even a digital one — can translate everything, including the mystery of the person, into data and performance. The risk of dehumanization — of building a future that excludes God and reduces the other to a means — is an ancient and ever-new temptation that today takes on a technical guise. Instead, let us choose the “way of Nehemiah,” which highlights the importance of working together to make the City of God a safe place for returning exiles. Rebuilding today means recognizing that, precisely from the plurality of voices and visions which, even though they sometimes remind us of the confusion caused by the diversity of spoken languages, a bright possibility emerges. Indeed, this is the possibility of building together, of transforming diversity into a resource and of making listening and dialogue the common ground upon which to cultivate justice and fraternity. Within this shared task, Christians discover their unique role of guiding actions toward God so that, in his light, pluralism does not dissipate into disorder, but instead, through the practice of synodality, it becomes the space in which humanity rediscovers its solid foundations and its final end. In the Book of Revelation, John sees the New Jerusalem “coming down out of heaven from God” (Rev 21:2) as a gift for all humanity. And this vision of grace is an invitation for us Christians to work together in order to foster a peaceful, just and dignified life in community within today’s “cities.”
¶ 10
因此，我們應避免「巴貝耳症候群」：即犧牲弱者的利潤崇拜、抹平差異的劃一性，以及那妄稱單一語言——即使是數碼語言——便可以將一切，包括人格的奧秘，化約為數據和表現的傲慢。非人性化的危機——建造一個排除天主、把他人化約為手段的未來——是一個古老而恆新的誘惑，它今日披上了科技的外衣。讓我們選擇「乃赫米雅之道」：強調共同合作，使天主之城成為流亡歸來者的安全居所。今日的重建，意味着承認：正是從那有時令我們想起語言混亂的多元聲音與視野之中，一個光明的可能性正在浮現——這是一同建設、把差異化為資源、以聆聽與對話為共同基礎以培育正義與兄弟情誼的可能。在這項共同的事業中，基督徒發現其獨特的角色：將行動導向天主，使多元在祂的光照下不致渙散為混亂，而是透過共議性的實踐，成為人類重新找到其堅實根基與終向的空間。在《默示錄》中，若望看見新耶路撒冷「從天上由天主那裏降下」（默 21:2），作為對全人類的恩賜。這恩寵的異象，是對我們基督徒的一個邀請：齊心合力，在今日的種種「城市」中，培育和平、正義、有尊嚴的社群生活。
Building for the common good
為公益而興建
¶ 11
Building a city founded on the common good implies, first and foremost, building on a firm relationship with God. It means recognizing that the truth of his love calls us to life “in all its fullness” ( Jn 10:10) and communion with him. Like Saint Augustine, we too can say, “You have made us for yourself, O Lord, and our heart is restless until it rests in you.” [8] Indeed, God has inscribed in our hearts a desire for happiness that embraces all the dimensions of life. The Church, in dialogue with the men and women of our time, recognizes the urgent need to safeguard and guide this aspiration toward its deepest truth.
¶ 11
建立一個以公益為基礎的城，首先意味着建基於與天主穩固的關係之上。它意味着承認：祂愛的真理召叫我們進入「豐盛的」生命（若 10:10），並與祂共融。正如聖奧斯定所言，我們也可以說：「上主，禰造了我們是為了禰；我們的心如不安息於禰，便不會得到安寧。」[8] 確實，天主已將對幸福的渴求銘刻於我們心中——這份渴求擁抱生命的一切層面。教會在與當代男女的對話中，認識到我們有迫切的需要去守護並引導這份渴望，使它走向其至深的真理。
¶ 12
Secondly, building for the common good means accepting the limits and weakness of humanity without considering them an error to be corrected. Today, the human desire for fullness of life is at risk of being misled by deceitful goals, such as the prospect of a technology that promises to free us from all weakness, and models of wellbeing that leave behind entire populations. All too often, we place our hope in unlimited “upgrades,” in forms of progress that exacerbate inequalities, and in immediate solutions incapable of healing people’s wounds. As a result, while some pursue the illusion of unlimited self-assertion, many are deprived of basic necessities. The Church reminds us, with a firm yet humble voice, that true fulfilment is not achieved by eliminating weakness but through harmonious growth. It is found where freedom and responsibility are intertwined with mutual care and true solidarity, and where progress is measured by the dignity of each person and the good of all peoples.
¶ 12
其次，為公益而興建意味着接納人性的限度和軟弱，不視之為需要修正的錯誤。今日，人對生命圓滿的渴求，正冒着被虛偽目標所誤導的危險：例如那承諾能將我們從一切軟弱中解脫的科技前景，或那將整批人口拋諸腦後的安適模式。我們常常把希望寄託於無止境的「升級」、加劇不平等的進步形式，以及那些無能醫治人傷痕的即時方案。其結果是：當有些人追逐着無限自我肯定的幻象時，許多人卻被剝奪了基本的所需。教會以堅定而謙卑的聲音提醒我們：真正的成全並非藉消除軟弱而達致，而是藉和諧的成長而獲得。它存於自由與責任，與相互關懷和真誠團結，交織之處；存於以每個人的尊嚴和諸民族的福祉為衡量的進步當中。
¶ 13
Thirdly, building a world in which everyone can flourish requires shared responsibility and courage. No one can single-handedly bear the weight of the challenges the world is facing, just as no one is so weak that they cannot play their part, for “power is made perfect in weakness” (2 Cor 12:9). All are given their own section of the wall: scientists and researchers, entrepreneurs and workers, educators and legislators, civil society, popular movements and faith communities. This is the logic of subsidiarity, which values the cooperation between generations, peoples, disciplines and cultures as the best way for fostering stability, prosperity and peace. We should not be intimidated by tensions or differences because they can become creative forces when guided by shared responsibility.
¶ 13
第三，建設一個人人皆能興盛的世界，需要共同的責任和勇氣。沒有任何一個人能獨自承擔世界所面對的這些挑戰的重量；同樣，沒有任何人軟弱到不能盡其一份力，因為「我的德能在軟弱中纔全顯出來」（格後 12:9）。每一個人都分得屬於自己的那段城牆：科學家與研究員、企業家與工人、教育家與立法者、公民社會、民間運動，以及信仰團體。這便是輔助性原則的邏輯——它珍視世代、民族、學科和文化之間的合作，視之為孕育安定、繁榮與和平的最佳途徑。我們不該被張力或差異所嚇倒，因為當這些張力與差異由共同的責任引導時，便能成為富創造力的力量。
¶ 14
Finally, building for the common good requires an evangelical language. We must avoid humiliating or antagonistic words, opting rather for a clarity that sheds light and a frankness that unlocks new possibilities. We cannot condone naïve enthusiasms, nor fuel unfounded fears. Instead, let us establish standards for discernment — the dignity of the human person, the universal destination of goods, the preferential option for the poor, care for our common home and peace — and let us translate these standards into practices such as responsible planning, the assessment of human and social impact, the inclusion of the most vulnerable, the promotion of digital literacy and guiding research and industry toward justice and peace.
¶ 14
最後，為公益而興建需要一種福音性的語言。我們必須避免羞辱性或對抗性的言辭，而選擇能照亮的清晰與能開啟新可能的坦率。我們不能縱容天真的狂熱，也不能助長毫無根據的恐懼。讓我們確立辨明的準則——人格的尊嚴、財富的普世用途、優先選擇貧者、照顧我們共同家園、和平——並讓我們把這些準則化為實踐：負責任的規劃、人文與社會影響的評估、納入最脆弱者、推動數碼素養、引導研究和產業走向正義與和平。
Remaining human
保持人性
¶ 15
In the recent Ordinary Jubilee Year of 2025, we walked as pilgrims of hope and were blessed with many graces. Strengthened by these gifts, we can move forward with confidence to face the arduous tasks and demanding challenges that lie ahead. In the era of artificial intelligence, when human dignity is threatened by new forms of dehumanization, ours is the pressing duty to remain profoundly human. We must lovingly safeguard the grandeur of humanity bestowed upon us and revealed in its fullness in Christ, the splendor of which no machine can ever replace. True progress always stems from a heart open to others, an intelligence willing to listen and a will that seeks what unites rather than what separates.
¶ 15
在剛過去的二○二五年常規禧年中，我們以「希望的朝聖者」的身分前行，並蒙獲眾多恩寵。藉這些恩賜的堅固，我們可以滿懷信心，前去面對橫亘前路的艱辛任務和苛嚴挑戰。在人工智能的年代，當人的尊嚴正被新形式的非人性化所威脅之際，我們的責任迫切：保持深刻的人性。我們必須以愛去守護那賜給我們、並在基督內以圓滿向我們啟示的人性壯麗——這份光輝，是任何機器都無從取代的。真正的進步常源自一顆向他人敞開的心，一種樂於聆聽的智慧，以及一份尋求那合一而非分裂之事物的意志。
¶ 16
I address this heartfelt appeal to all the Catholic faithful, to all Christians and to all men and women of goodwill. Let us not be afraid to get our hands dirty on the “construction site” of our time. Like Nehemiah, let us pray, plan wisely and work perseveringly, placing God at the forefront of our actions and the human person at the center of our choices. Thus, the “rejected stones” — the poor, the sick, the migrants and the least among us — will become the cornerstone, and a solid, welcoming common home will emerge on the earth, where love and faithfulness will finally meet, and righteousness and peace will embrace (cf. Ps 85:10). This is the blessing we implore from God; and the task that stands before us is that of being builders of communion, rather than architects of Babel. We are to be servants of the coming Kingdom, instead of lords of towers destined for ruin. With the heart of a shepherd and a father, I ask everyone to abandon the construction of yet another Tower of Babel and to join forces in building up the common good, so that humanity will never lose its beauty, and the world once again will come to recognize the human heart as the place where God desires to dwell.
¶ 16
我向所有公教信眾、所有基督徒、所有善心的男女，發出這份由衷的呼籲。讓我們不要害怕在這個時代的「工地」上弄髒雙手。讓我們效法乃赫米雅：祈禱、明智地計劃、堅毅地工作，把天主置於我們行動的首位，把人放在我們抉擇的中心。如此，那些「被棄置的石頭」——貧者、病者、移民、最微小者——將成為棟梁；一個堅實而好客的共同家園將在大地上湧現，在那裏「仁愛和忠信必彼此相迎，正義與和平必互相親吻」（參詠 85:10）。這便是我們向天主祈求的祝福；而擺在我們眼前的任務是：作共融的建造者，而非巴貝耳的設計師；作那即將來臨之神國的僕人，而非那注定傾倒之諸塔的主子。懷着一顆牧者與父親的心，我懇請每一個人：放下另一座巴貝耳塔的興建，攜手共同建設公益；如此，人類將永不失去其美麗，世界亦將再次認識到：人的心，正是天主願居住之地。
CHAPTER ONE · 第一章

A DYNAMIC APPROACH FAITHFUL TO THE GOSPEL

忠於福音的動態進路

· · ·
¶ 17
In this first chapter, I intend to present synthetically how the Social Doctrine of the Church has taken shape in the recent Papal Magisterium and in the Second Vatican Council, in order to demonstrate its dynamic character. Indeed, in each era the res novae require that this teaching address historical questions in the light of revealed Truth. In this regard, artificial intelligence, too, should not be considered as merely yet another theme to be studied or a crisis to be managed, but rather as a development that challenges the categories of Social Doctrine from within, calling for their further development in fidelity to the Gospel.
¶ 17
在這第一章中，我打算綜合地闡述教會社會訓導如何在近代教宗訓導當局及梵蒂岡第二屆大公會議中逐步形成，以展示其動態的特質。事實上，在每一個時代，**res novae**（新事物）都要求這項訓導在啟示真理的光照下，回應歷史提出的問題。就此而言，人工智能也不應僅被視為又一個有待研究的主題，或一場有待處理的危機，而應被視為一種從內部挑戰社會訓導諸範疇的發展，要求我們在忠於福音的前提下，對這些範疇作出進一步的發展。
¶ 18
This overview, however, would not be very comprehensible if, before reflecting on the contribution of individual popes and their most relevant documents, we do not first clarify some fundamental principles concerning the way in which the Church exists in history and relates to the world. Failing to do so would expose Social Doctrine to the risk of being perceived as an undue interference in “worldly” matters or as an external code of ethics imposed from above. In reality, it stems from a Church that walks alongside humanity, recognizing the autonomy of earthly realities and the distinction between ecclesial and political communities. Indeed, it is for this very reason that she strives to serve the common good.
¶ 18
然而，在我們反思歷任教宗個人及其最重要文件的貢獻之前，若不曾先闡明關於教會在歷史中存在並與世界建立關係的方式的若干基本原則，這番回顧便不太容易理解。若不如此，便會使教會社會訓導面臨被視為對「世俗」事務的不當干涉，或一套從上而下強加的外在倫理規範的風險。事實上，它源自一個與人類同行的教會，她承認現世現實的自主性，以及教會團體與政治團體之間的區別。的確，正是為此緣故，她竭力服務公益。
A Church journeying through human history
與人類歷史同行的教會
¶ 19
The Church is present in the world as a sign of unity for the entire human family. She recognizes today’s questions and challenges as the current setting in which to carry out her particular vocation of listening, dialogue and service, and of being responsive to everything concerning the lives of contemporary men and women. This involvement in people’s lives helps the Church understand ever more clearly that her mission has a historical scope and entails a responsibility for the way in which social relations are built. For this reason, she cannot consider herself a stranger to the forces shaping society. On the contrary, the Church actively participates in the processes by which society grows and is organized, and she offers her own contribution to the creation of a more just and fraternal society. Pope Francis emphasized this historical dimension of the Church’s mission: “No one can demand that religion should be relegated to the inner sanctum of personal life, without influence on societal and national life, without concern for the soundness of civil institutions, without a right to offer an opinion on events affecting society.” [9]
¶ 19
教會臨在於世界，作為整個人類大家庭合一的標記。她體認到今日的種種疑問與挑戰，正是她履行其獨特聖召的當前環境——那便是聆聽、交談與服務，並對當代男女生活所涉及的一切作出回應。這種對人們生活的投入，幫助教會日益清晰地領悟到，她的使命具有歷史的幅度，並蘊含著對社會關係構建方式的責任。為此緣故，她不能自視為塑造社會各種力量的旁觀者。相反地，教會積極參與社會成長與組織的進程，並為創建一個更公義、更友愛的社會獻上自己的貢獻。教宗方濟各強調了教會使命的這一歷史幅度：「沒有人能要求宗教被貶抑至個人生活的內在聖所，對社會和國家生活不產生影響，不關心公民體制的健全，無權對影響社會的事件發表意見。」[9]
¶ 20
The Church’s vocation and duty to accompany humanity in the specifics of history leads her to recognize that earthly realities possess their own proper character and order. The Second Vatican Council expressed this principle with particular precision in the Pastoral Constitution Gaudium et Spes, whose sixtieth anniversary we remembered and celebrated with gratitude on 7 December 2025: “If by the autonomy of earthly affairs is meant that created things and societies themselves enjoy their own laws and values… then the demand for autonomy is perfectly in order.” [10] This affirmation shows that creation bears the imprint of an original goodness that our human outlook must preserve, cultivate and bring to fulfilment. In this regard, the Church offers herself in a way that helps to interpret reality in all its depth. She supports with humble firmness the choices that promote the dignity of every person, the cohesion of communities and the good of all. The Church thus stands alongside the world without overpowering it, so that the promise of justice and peace that the Holy Spirit continues to sustain in the heart of humanity may come to fruition in every human endeavor.
¶ 20
教會在歷史的具體處境中陪伴人類的使命與責任，使她認識到現世事物具有其固有的特性和秩序。梵蒂岡第二屆大公會議在《論教會在現代世界》牧職憲章（*Gaudium et Spes*）中，以格外精確的方式表達了這一原則——我們懷著感恩之心，於2025年12月7日紀念並慶祝了該憲章頒布六十週年：「所謂現世事務的自主，如果是指受造物和社會團體本身享有其自身的規律和價值……那麼，要求這種自主是完全合理的。」[10] 這一肯定表明，創造帶有原始美善的印記，我們人類的目光必須保存、培養並使之達至圓滿。在這方面，教會以一種有助於深入詮釋現實的方式奉獻自己。她以謙遜而堅定的態度支持那些促進每一個人尊嚴、團體凝聚力及眾人福祉的抉擇。教會因此立於世界之旁而不凌駕其上，好使聖神持續在人性心中維繫的正義與和平的許諾，能在人類的每一項努力中結出果實。
¶ 21
Recognizing that God upholds the freedom of men and women in the unfolding of history, the Second Vatican Council affirmed the distinction between the ecclesial community and the political community, emphasizing that each must operate with full autonomy. The Church’s presence in the world is also expressed through her relationship with civil society and public institutions. By engaging with these entities, the Church acknowledges the value of social and political realities and honors their specific responsibilities, supporting everything that fosters the wellbeing of individuals and strengthens the fabric of society. The Church does not claim to assume the functions belonging to the State. On the contrary, she esteems those who serve the common good, and she firmly acknowledges the responsibility that civil institutions hold within society. At the same time, the mission entrusted to the Church prompts her to address the real suffering of the men and women of our time. This closeness does not stem from an intent to supplant civil institutions, much less from an implicit criticism of their work. Rather, it stems from evangelical charity, which impels the Church to draw near to the wounds of humanity whenever they surface with greater severity. When the Church intervenes, she does so following the example of the Good Samaritan, with discretion and closeness, aware that what arises from urgent necessity cannot become the norm, nor replace the institutional responsibilities proper to the civil community.
¶ 21
梵蒂岡第二屆大公會議確認天主在歷史的演進中維護男女的自由，同時申明教會團體與政治團體之間的區別，強調兩者必須完全自主地運作。教會在世界的臨在，也透過她與公民社會及公共機構的關係表達出來。透過與這些實體的交往，教會承認社會和政治現實的價值，尊重它們各自的責任，並支持一切促進個人福祉及強化社會結構的事務。教會並不意圖承擔屬於國家的職能。相反地，她敬重那些為公益服務的人，並堅定地承認公民機構在社會中所肩負的責任。與此同時，託付給教會的使命催迫她回應我們這時代男女的實際苦難。這種關懷並非出於取代公民機構的意圖，更非隱含對其工作的批評。相反地，這是源於福音的愛德，這愛德驅使教會每當人類的創傷以更大嚴重性顯露時，便走近這些傷口。當教會介入時，她效法善牧的榜樣，以謹慎和關懷的態度行事，深知出於迫切需要的行動不能成為常規，也不能取代屬於公民團體的體制責任。
¶ 22
Starting from this twofold acknowledgment — the autonomy of earthly realities and the distinction between ecclesiastical and political spheres of competence — allows for a clearer understanding of the direction that the Second Vatican Council set for the Church in her relationship with the world. Gaudium et Spes reminds us that “it is the task of the whole People of God, particularly of its pastors and theologians, to listen to and distinguish the many voices of our times and to interpret them in the light of God’s word, in order that the revealed Truth may be more deeply penetrated, better understood and more suitably presented.” [11] Listening to the “many voices” is no mere sociological exercise, but instead requires spiritual discernment. Guided by the Spirit, the People of God come to recognize in cultural and social transformations both the signs of the presence of Christ, who comes and guides history toward its fulfilment, and those aberrations that obscure his face. In this way, the essential core of revealed Truth is not altered, but made explicit and adopted as a living standard for guiding concrete choices, inspiring paths of personal and communal conversion, promoting structural reforms and supporting new forms of evangelical witness in public life. History is thus understood as one of the places in which the Church allows herself to be taught by the Spirit about the humanizing power of the Gospel; and she learns to develop her own teaching at the service of the dignity of every person and the good of all peoples.
¶ 22
從這雙重承認出發——即現世現實的自主性，以及教會領域與政治領域職權範圍的區分——我們可以更清晰地理解梵蒂岡第二屆大公會議為教會所設定、在其與世界的關係中應循的方向。《論教會在現代世界》牧職憲章提醒我們：「全體天主子民——尤其是牧者與神學家——的任務，是聆聽並分辨我們時代的種種聲音，並在天主聖言的光照下加以詮釋，好使啟示的真理能更深入地為人所領悟、更妥善地為人所理解、更合宜地為人所呈現。」[11] 聆聽「種種聲音」絕非僅僅是一項社會學的操練，而是需要屬靈的分辨。在聖神的引導下，天主子民在文化與社會的轉變中，既能認出基督臨在的標記——祂正在來臨，並引導歷史走向其圓滿實現——也能辨別那些遮蔽祂面容的偏差。如此，啟示真理的核心本質並未被改變，反而得以顯明，並被採納為活生生的準則，用以引導具體的抉擇、激發個人與團體皈依的途徑、推動結構性的改革，並支持在公共生活中以福音作證的新形式。歷史因此被理解為教會容讓自己受教於聖神的場所之一，從中學習福音使人成聖的人性化力量；教會也在其中學習發展自己的訓導，以服務每一個人的尊嚴和所有民族的福祉。
The wisdom of the word of God in dialogue with the human sciences
與人文科學對話的天主聖言之智慧
¶ 23
The Church regards all who sincerely seek “truth, goodness and beauty” as companions on the journey, and considers them as “precious allies” [12] in defending the dignity of every person and in caring for creation. Adopting the pastoral approach of the Second Vatican Council, which invites us to listen, discern and interpret the signs of the times, and enlightened by the wisdom of the word, the Church is not afraid to encounter human knowledge. Indeed, the word of God provides reliable standards for establishing paths of justice and opening ways of reconciliation and peace among peoples. When it comes to applying these standards to the complex situations of our time, the contributions of philosophy and of the human and social sciences is essential. These disciplines help us understand and analyze cultural, economic and political dynamics more deeply. Saint John Paul II recalled that the Church welcomes the contributions of the social sciences in order “to draw from them concrete insights that help her carry out her magisterial office.” [13] A dialogue with such kinds of knowledge does not diminish the power of the Gospel. On the contrary, it makes it possible to identify with greater clarity what genuinely fosters the lives of individuals and communities. Following this perspective, Pope Francis emphasized that when dealing with many specific questions, the Church does not claim to offer “a definitive opinion,” [14] but recognizes the importance of listening to scientific research and of encouraging a serious and honest debate among experts while welcoming a diversity of opinions.
¶ 23
教會視所有真誠尋求「真、善、美」的人為旅途上的同伴，並將他們視為「寶貴的盟友」[12]，共同捍衛每一個人的尊嚴，關懷受造界。教會採納梵蒂岡第二屆大公會議的牧民方針——邀請我們聆聽、分辨和詮釋時代的徵兆，並在天主聖言的智慧光照下——毫不畏懼與人類知識相遇。事實上，天主的聖言提供了可靠的準則，以建立正義的道路，並在民族之間開闢和解與和平的途徑。當需要將這些準則應用於我們時代的複雜處境時，哲學以及人文和社會科學的貢獻是不可或缺的。這些學科幫助我們更深入地理解和分析文化、經濟和政治的動態。聖若望保祿二世曾提醒我們，教會接納社會科學的貢獻，是為了「從中汲取具體的洞見，以協助她履行其訓導職務。」[13] 與這些知識領域的對話，並不會減損福音的力量。相反地，它使我們能夠更清晰地辨識出什麼才是真正促進個人和團體生活的事物。依循此一觀點，教宗方濟各強調，在處理許多具體問題時，教會並不聲稱能提供「一個決定性的意見」[14]，而是承認聆聽科學研究、鼓勵專家之間進行嚴肅而誠實的辯論，並在接納多元意見的同時，均具有其重要性。
¶ 24
Nourished by this fruitful dialogue between the Gospel and human knowledge, the Church has progressively developed her Social Doctrine, cultivating in history a wise patrimony marked by theological and anthropological coherence rooted in the Christian understanding of the person. Precisely because this patrimony arises from faith and a corresponding vision of reality, it does not amount to a repertoire of technical solutions or an economic or political model to be set against others. Instead, it belongs to a different order, [15] namely that of the principles that guide the interpretation of events and sustain an evangelical understanding of historical processes and the choices these entail. Herein lies the proper function of Social Doctrine, which does not claim to supplant the responsibilities of politics or institutions, but offers itself as a foundation for collective discernment, helping to recognize and promote whatever serves the dignity of persons, the vitality of communities and the common good.
¶ 24
在福音與人類知識之間這種豐碩對話的滋養下，教會逐步發展了她的社會訓導，在歷史中培育出一份睿智的遺產，其特色是建基於基督信仰對人的理解之上的神學與人學連貫性。正因為這份遺產源自信仰以及與之相應的現實觀，它並非一套技術解決方案彙編，也不是一個用來對抗其他模式的經濟或政治模式。相反地，它屬於另一個層次，[15] 即指導我們詮釋事件的原則層次，並支持我們以福音精神理解歷史進程及其所帶來的抉擇。這正是社會訓導的固有功能：它無意取代政治或制度的責任，而是提供一個集體分辨的基礎，幫助我們辨認並促進一切有助於人格尊嚴、團體活力與公益的事物。
Social Doctrine as a shared discernment
作為共同辨明的社會訓導
¶ 25
Understanding that the truth is a gift to be shared, not a possession to be monopolized, frees the Church from the temptation of seeking forms of presence based on power. In order to rediscover the evangelical approach of a gentle proclamation of truth that is not imposed, Saint John Paul II invited us to examine honestly the times when acquiescence was given to “intolerance and even the use of violence in the service of truth.” [16] In this same vein, I too have reaffirmed that the Church “does not claim to possess a monopoly on truth,” [17] because truth is not a territory to be defended, but a good to be shared. For his part, Pope Francis expressed this same perspective in his striking phrase, “time is greater than space.” [18] What matters most is not occupying positions of power or defending cultural strongholds, but initiating good processes and enabling them to mature. In this way, the truth of the Gospel is not imposed from above, but grows over time within the concrete interweaving of lives, communities and cultures. This is not a truth that fears diversity, but instead welcomes and guides it. It does not eliminate conflicts, but transforms them, reuniting that which history tends to scatter. This concept can also be illustrated by the image of a multifaceted polyhedron, [19] in which the one truth of the Gospel is reflected from different angles.
¶ 25
明白真理是一份需要分享的禮物，而非一項需要壟斷的擁有物，這使教會免受誘惑，不去謀求那些立基於權力的臨在形式。為了重新發現那種溫柔宣講真理、而非強加於人的福音方式，聖若望保祿二世邀請我們誠實地省察那些曾屈服於「不寬容，甚至為真理服務而使用暴力」[16] 的時刻。循著同樣的精神，我也曾重申，教會「並不宣稱對真理擁有壟斷權」[17]，因為真理並非一片需要捍衛的領土，而是一份需要分享的美善。教宗方濟各則以他一句意味深長的話表達了這同一觀點：「時間大於空間。」[18] 最重要的不是佔據權力位置或捍衛文化堡壘，而是啟動良好的進程並使其日趨成熟。這樣，福音的真理並非自上而下強加於人，而是在具體交織的生活、團體和文化中隨著時間而成長。這並非一個畏懼多樣性的真理，相反地，它接納並引導多樣性。它不消除衝突，而是轉化衝突，將歷史趨向於分散的事物重新聚合起來。這個概念也可以用一個多面體的形象來說明[19]，在其中，福音的同一真理從不同的角度被反映出來。
¶ 26
This attitude of openness to truth, which is at the same time both one and diverse, profoundly expresses the catholicity of the Church, for she embraces the entire human family yet is also immersed in the concrete situations of peoples and cultures. The Second Vatican Council reminds us that, in virtue of this very catholicity, “each part contributes its own gifts to other parts and to the entire Church.” [20] In this way, the Church grows as a whole and as individual communities thanks to a mutual exchange and to shared efforts toward an ever fuller communion. It follows, then, that the People of God are not only gathered together from many peoples, but are also intertwined through different functions, vocations, cultures and traditions, each being called to support and enrich one another. From this perspective, Saint Paul VI acknowledged that, given the great variety of historical situations, it is unrealistic to think that the Church’s Social Doctrine can propose a single response that is valid in all contexts. [21] For this reason, he invited each Christian community to interpret the reality in its own country with clarity and responsibility. The fruitful tension between the universality of the Church’s mission and her local roots is an intrinsic aspect of her life, for she encompasses the whole world, while addressing the specific issues of each context as the real setting in which the Gospel takes shape.
¶ 26
這種同時既是一體又是多元的向真理開放的態度，深刻地體現了教會的大公性，因為她既懷抱整個人類大家庭，卻又置身於各民族與文化具體的境況之中。梵蒂岡第二屆大公會議提醒我們，正是憑藉這大公性，「每一部分都向其他部分及整個教會貢獻自己的禮物。」[20] 如此，教會透過彼此交流以及為邁向更圓滿的共融而共同努力，得以作為一個整體和作為個別團體而成長。由此可見，天主子民不僅由眾多民族聚集而成，更透過不同的職務、聖召、文化與傳統交織在一起，每一份子都蒙召去支持和豐富彼此。從這個角度來看，聖保祿六世承認，鑑於歷史處境的多樣性，若以為教會社會訓導能夠提出一個在所有環境中都適用的單一回應，那是不切實際的。[21] 為此，他邀請每一個基督徒團體，以清晰和責任心去解讀自己國家的現實。教會使命的普世性與地方根源之間富有成果的張力，是她生命的內在本質，因為她既涵蓋整個世界，同時又回應每一個處境中的具體問題，以之作為福音具體成形的真實場所。
¶ 27
In light of what has been said so far, the Church’s Social Doctrine can be seen more authentically. It is not a handbook of principles and norms to be applied, but a process of shared discernment. It is born from the encounter between the eternal truth of the Gospel and the questions of history. It allows itself to be challenged by the signs of the times, and draws nourishment from the contributions of science, culture and human experience. Therefore, when the dignity of our brothers and sisters is violated, when politics fails to address the tragedies of humanity, when the economy turns against the person or science oversteps the limits of its competence, [22] the Church — together with other Christian denominations and believers of other religions — must make her voice heard, not in order to dominate, but to promote communion. Understood in this way, Social Doctrine becomes a theology of communion in history, a history in which the Word made flesh continues to be present through dialogue, memory and prophecy.
¶ 27
鑑於以上所述，我們可以更真切地理解教會的社會訓導。它不是一本供人應用的原則與規範手冊，而是一項共同分辨的進程。它誕生於福音的永恆真理與歷史的提問之間的相遇。它讓自己接受時代徵兆的挑戰，並從科學、文化及人類經驗的貢獻中汲取滋養。因此，當我們弟兄姊妹的尊嚴遭受侵犯時，當政治無法應對人類的悲劇時，當經濟反過來壓迫人，或科學逾越其權限時，[22] 教會——連同其他基督宗派及其他宗教的信徒——必須發出自己的聲音，不是為支配他人，而是為促進共融。如此理解之下，社會訓導便成為歷史中的一門共融神學，而在這段歷史中，聖言成了血肉通過交談、記憶與先知之言，持續臨在其中。
The development of Social Doctrine from Leo XIII to the present
教會社會訓導自良十三世以來的發展
¶ 28
Having outlined the way in which the Church is present in history and engages in dialogue with the world, I would now like to consider the development of Social Doctrine in the Magisterium, which has responded to the major social transformations from the nineteenth century to the present day. Naturally, I cannot do justice to the full richness of this teaching, whose fundamental principles are presented in the Compendium of the Social Doctrine of the Church and have been further examined by recent Magisterial teaching. Nor can I systematically explore everything that has been developed in the Encyclicals of my late venerable predecessors, especially in Laudato Si’and Fratelli Tutti. Nevertheless, I will emphasize some essential points in order to show how the present text stands in continuity with that tradition. I would also like to stress how, within this tradition, the unchanging core of revealed truths regarding the human person and society is constantly intertwined with a renewed capacity for listening to historical situations and for responding to contemporary issues. I will now review some of the significant stages of this development, beginning with the period inaugurated by the Encyclical Rerum Novarum.
¶ 28
在概述了教會如何在歷史中存在並與世界對話之後，我現在希望考察教會訓導中社會訓導的發展，這訓導回應了從十九世紀至今的各項重大社會轉變。當然，我無法完全展現這項教導的全部豐富內容；其基本原則已在《教會社會訓導彙編》中論述，並由近期的訓導文件進一步探討。我也無法系統地探討我可敬的前任教宗們在通諭中所闡述的一切，特別是在《願祢受讚頌》和《眾位弟兄》中的內容。儘管如此，我將強調若干要點，以顯示本文本如何與該傳統一脈相承。我也希望強調，在此傳統中，關乎人及社會的啟示真理的不變核心，是如何不斷地與一種更新的能力交織在一起的——這能力就是聆聽歷史處境，並回應當代議題。我現在將回顧這發展過程中的若干重要階段，從《新事》通諭所開啟的時期開始。
The first stages of the Church’s Social Doctrine
教會社會訓導的最初階段
CHAPTER TWO · 第二章

FOUNDATIONS AND PRINCIPLES OF THE SOCIAL DOCTRINE OF THE CHURCH

教會社會訓導的基礎與原則

· · ·
¶ 46
The Social Doctrine of the Church is a living reality, in dialogue with history, cultures and sciences. At the same time, it enshrines a core set of unchanging truths. For this reason, it can be considered a form of wisdom that is capable of guiding the personal and societal lives of believers even today. In this second chapter, I would like to focus on some of the foundations and principles of the Church’s Social Doctrine that will help us to interpret the “new things” of our time, particularly in view of the inherent dignity of the human person. In order to protect the human person in the age of artificial intelligence, I believe that today we must once again reflect on the common good, the universal destination of goods, subsidiarity, solidarity and social justice. I am convinced that a harmonious relationship between these principles requires that they be considered collectively, so that it becomes clear how they relate to and complement each other.
¶ 46
教會社會訓導是一個活生生的現實，與歷史、文化和科學持續對話。與此同時，它蘊含著一套不可改變的核心真理。為此，它可以被視為一種智慧，即使在今日，也能夠引導信眾的個人生活和社會生活。在這第二章中，我想集中探討教會社會訓導的某些基礎和原則，它們將幫助我們詮釋我們時代的「新事物」，特別著眼於人位格與生俱來的尊嚴。為了在人工智能時代保護人位格，我認為今天我們必須再次省思公益、財物的普遍歸向、輔助原則、團結關懷，以及社會正義。我深信，這些原則之間的和諧關係，要求我們將它們集體地考量，好能清楚地看出它們如何互相關聯和彼此補足。
¶ 47
In offering these reflections, my hope is, first and foremost, to help the lay faithful and people of goodwill rediscover their duty of implementing the above-mentioned principles in their daily lives, family relationships, work and involvement in society. Thus, they will let themselves be inspired by the aim of embodying God’s love in the concrete events of life. At the same time, I would like to encourage academic institutions and universities to give fresh impetus to these principles, and to apply them in a way that will be relevant and effective in addressing the digital revolution. In this way, theological and philosophical enquiry will be able to further explore and support the Church’s pastoral journey, and contribute to the Magisterium’s task of enlightening the consciences of the faithful and guiding their efforts to make the life of our societies more just and fraternal.
¶ 47
我提出這些反思，首先和最重要的希望是幫助平信徒和善心人士，重新發現他們在日常生活、家庭關係、工作和社會參與中，實踐上述原則的責任。這樣，他們將讓自己受到在生活的具體事件中體現天主聖愛這一目標所啟發。與此同時，我願鼓勵學術機構和大學，為這些原則注入新的動力，並以切合和有效的方式應用它們來應對數碼革命。如此，神學和哲學的探索將能進一步深化和支持教會的牧民旅程，並為教會訓導當局光照信友良心、引導他們努力使我們的社會生活更加公義和友愛的任務作出貢獻。
The foundations of Social Doctrine
社會訓導的基礎
The human person: image of the Triune God
人類：三位一體天主的肖像
¶ 48
The Church’s Social Doctrine brings us to the very heart of our faith: the mystery of the living God, revealed in Jesus Christ, who, as a communion of Persons — Father, Son and Holy Spirit — is love itself in relationship, expressed in the mutual gift of self and in sharing with the world. [51] As the Council recalled, human persons are called to communion with God and “can fully discover their true selves only in sincere self-giving.” [52] Indeed their deepest vocation is to enter into the Trinitarian dynamic of love received and shared.
¶ 48
教會社會訓導將我們帶到信仰的核心：生活的天主的奧蹟，即在耶穌基督內啟示出來的天主，祂作為位格的共融——聖父、聖子及聖神——是關係中的愛本身，並在彼此的自我交付和與世界的分享中表達出來。[51] 正如大公會議所提醒的，人被召叫與天主共融，並且「只有在真誠的自我交付中，才能完全發現自己的真實自我。」[52] 事實上，人最深的聖召就是進入那接受並分享的愛——聖三的愛的動力之中。
¶ 49
If the mystery of God as Love is the source of Social Doctrine, we see its most concrete expression in the face of Jesus Christ, the Incarnate Word. By becoming man, the Son of God enters our history and takes on human flesh, bringing with him the love that unites him to the Father and the Holy Spirit. In him, “the mystery of humanity truly becomes clear” [53] because his humanity is completely free, open to others, capable of building healthy and beautiful relationships and committed to the total gift of self. Those who believe in him are engaged in the great work of renewal that began with the mystery of his passion, death and resurrection, and they cooperate in building up the Kingdom of God, learning to embrace all men and women as brothers and sisters, children of one Father. In this way, both the proclamation of the Gospel and Christian life, guided by the action of the Holy Spirit, tend to bring about social consequences in the world. [54]
¶ 49
倘若天主是愛這奧蹟乃教會社會訓導的泉源，那麼我們便在耶穌基督——降生成人的聖言——的面容上，看到這奧蹟最具體的表述。天主子藉著成為人，進入我們的歷史，取了人的血肉，並將那使祂與聖父及聖神合一的爱帶給我們。在祂內，「人性的奧蹟得以真正彰顯」[53]，因為祂的人性是完全自由的、向他人開放的、能夠建立健康而美好的關係，並全然致力於自我的徹底交付。凡相信祂的人，都參與了那始於祂的苦難、死亡與復活奧蹟的偉大更新工程，並協力建設天主的國，學習接納所有男男女女為兄弟姊妹、同一天父的子女。這樣，無論是傳揚福音，抑或是受聖神行動所引導的基督徒生活，都傾向於在世間結出社會性的果實。[54]
¶ 50
At the heart of the Christian understanding of the human person lies the great biblical affirmation that men and women are created in the image and likeness (cf. Gen 1:26-27) of the Triune God. Created for relationship, every human person is planned and willed by God to enter into communion with him, with others and with creation. Human dignity does not depend on a person’s abilities, wealth or position in life, nor on the right or wrong choices made; instead, it is a gift that precedes and transcends each person, endowed by God as an expression of his unfailing love. For this reason, the human person always remains the “way for the Church” [55] and the heart of every authentic path of integral human development. [56]
¶ 50
基督徒對人的理解的核心，在於聖經那偉大的肯定：男人和女人都是按照三位一體天主的肖像和模樣所造（參 Gen 1:26-27）。每一個人都為關係而受造，由天主所計劃、所願意，為進入與祂、與他人、與受造界的共融之中。人的尊嚴並不取決於一個人的能力、財富或社會地位，也不取決於他所做的是對或錯的選擇；相反，這是一份先於並超越每一個人的禮物，由天主所賜予，作為祂永恆不渝的愛的彰顯。為此，人永遠是「教會的道路」[55]，也是每一條通往整全人性發展的真實途徑的核心。[56]
The equal dignity of all human beings
人人尊嚴平等
¶ 51
Saint John Paul II stated that, “this heightened sense of the dignity of the human person and of his or her uniqueness, and of the respect due to the journey of conscience, certainly represents one of the positive achievements of modern culture.” [57] This statement follows the line already laid out by the Second Vatican Council, which had noted a growing recognition of the sublime dignity of all persons, their superiority over material things and their universal and inviolable rights and duties. [58] It is important to ensure that this growth in appreciation of human dignity is not obscured by the pressure of new ideologies or very powerful interests in today’s world. Among these ideologies, I consider particularly insidious the one that suggests that every person must earn or justify his or her own worth, to the point of attributing greater value to those who are more efficient or effective. From this perspective, persons end up being reduced to a means of achieving results, a resource to be used and exploited, and are no longer recognized as a proper end in themselves who should never be instrumentalized. The value of persons, however, does not depend on what they achieve or produce. There are rights that apply to everyone simply by virtue of being human, and no human power can legitimately deny or arbitrarily limit them. [59]
¶ 51
聖若望保祿二世指出：「對人格尊嚴及其獨特性，以及對良心歷程應有之尊重的高度意識，確實是現代文化的正面成果之一。」[57] 這一陳述遵循了梵蒂岡第二屆大公會議早已鋪設的路線，該會議注意到，人們日益認識到所有人的崇高尊嚴、其超越物質事物的優越性，以及其普遍而不可侵犯的權利與義務。[58] 重要的是，要確保這種對人性尊嚴日益增進的賞識，不會被當今世界的新意識形態或極其強大的利益所掩蓋。在這些意識形態中，我認為尤其陰險的一種，是那種暗示每一個人必須賺取或證明自身價值的想法，甚至演變為賦予那些更有效率或效用的人更大的價值。從這個角度來看，人最終被貶低為一種達成結果的工具、一種可供使用和剝削的資源，而不再被承認為一個本身即是目的、絕不應被工具化的存在。然而，人的價值並不取決於他們所成就或生產的東西。有些權利是單純因著身為人而適用於每一個人的，任何人間權力都不能合法地否認或任意地限制這些權利。[59]
¶ 52
When we speak of dignity, we do not always use the word in the same way. Sometimes we refer to moral dignity, namely the way in which a person directs his or her choices and actions. At other times, we think of social dignity, which refers to a person’s living conditions and the concrete respect received from society. In other cases, we refer to existential dignity, meaning the way in which a person perceives his or her own worth and the value of life. These aspects of dignity can be enhanced or diminished. In addition to these notions, there is also the more profound and important level of ontological dignity. This is the dignity that belongs to every human being simply by virtue of existing, of having been willed, created and loved by God. [60] No sin, failure, humiliation or exclusion can diminish the profound value of a human life that God has willed and called into being. [61]
¶ 52
當我們談論尊嚴時，我們並非總是以同樣的方式使用這個詞。有時我們指的是道德尊嚴，即一個人引導其選擇和行動的方式。有時我們想到的是社會尊嚴，這關乎一個人的生活條件以及從社會獲得的具體尊重。還有其他情況，我們指的是存在性尊嚴，意指一個人對自身價值和生命意義的感知方式。這些不同層面的尊嚴可以增進或減損。除了這些概念之外，還有更深刻、更重要的本體尊嚴層次。這尊嚴屬於每一個人，僅僅因為他存在，因為他蒙天主所願、所造、所愛。[60] 沒有任何罪過、失敗、羞辱或排斥，能減損一個蒙天主所願並召叫進入存有的生命之深厚價值。[61]
¶ 53
The fundamental dignity of each person, therefore, is neither acquired nor earned, nor does it need to be justified. The recent Declaration Dignitas Infinita offers a summary of the Church’s thinking on this subject: “Every human person possesses an infinite dignity, inalienably grounded in his or her very being, which prevails in and beyond every circumstance, state, or situation the person may ever encounter” [62] — in other words, always and without exception. The dignity of every human being can be described as infinite, as Saint John Paul II stated, [63] for two reasons: first, because the love of God, who calls us to friendship with him, is infinite; and second, his love is absolutely unconditional, in the sense that, even if we search endlessly, we will never find anything that can erase or deny it.
¶ 53
因此，每一個人的基本尊嚴，既非獲取而得，亦非憑功績賺得，更不需要為之辯護。最近的《無限尊嚴》宣言，為教會在這課題上的思想提供了一個撮要：「每一個人都擁有一種無限的尊嚴，不可剝奪地奠基於其自身的存有之上，這尊嚴在任何處境、狀態或情況中，無論其過去、現在或未來，都始終佔據主導地位」[62] —— 換言之，無時無刻，絕無例外。正如聖若望保祿二世所言，[63] 每個人的尊嚴可被形容為無限的，原因有二：首先，因為天主召叫我們與祂建立友誼的愛，是無限的；其次，祂的愛是絕對無條件的，意思是，即使我們無窮盡地尋找，也永遠找不到任何能夠抹去或否定這愛的事物。
The supreme value of human rights
人權的至高價值
¶ 54
The Church gratefully acknowledges that “the movement toward the identification and proclamation of human rights is one of the most significant attempts to respond effectively to the inescapable demands of human dignity.” [64] In this regard, Saint John Paul II stated that the Universal Declaration of Human Rights, proclaimed by the United Nations on 10 December 1948, remains one of the highest expressions of the human conscience of our time. [65] It is “a milestone on the long and difficult path of the human race.” [66] For this reason, from the Christian perspective, human rights are not an external addition to the person, but an expression of intrinsic human dignity, which the international community is called to protect and promote.
¶ 54
教會深懷感恩地確認：「辨認和宣告人權的運動，是有效回應人性尊嚴無可迴避的要求的最重要嘗試之一。」[64] 就此，聖若望保祿二世指出，聯合國於一九四八年十二月十日頒布的《世界人權宣言》，至今仍是我們這時代人類良知的最高表達之一。[65] 它是「人類漫長而艱難旅程上的一座里程碑」。[66] 為此，從基督信仰的角度來看，人權並非外加於人身之上的附加物，而是人性固有尊嚴的表達，國際社會有責任予以保護和促進。
¶ 55
Human rights are inviolable, since they are “inherent in the human person and in human dignity.” [67] Consequently, they are universal and inalienable. [68] Precisely because they are grounded in the common dignity of every man and woman, they have practical consequences and legal effects, for “it would be vain to proclaim human rights if, at the same time, everything were not done to ensure the duty of respecting them, respect by all, in all places and for all.” [69] Among these rights, the first is the right to life, from conception to its natural end, [70] without which it is impossible to exercise any other right. When this fundamental right is denied — as in the cases of induced abortion, killing of the innocent and euthanasia — we are faced with choices that the Church considers gravely wrong. [71]
¶ 55
人權是不可侵犯的，因為它們「內在於人的位格與人性尊嚴」。[67] 因此，人權具有普世性且不可剝奪。[68] 正因為人權建基於每一個男人和女人的共同尊嚴之上，它們具有實際的後果和法律效力，因為「倘若不同時盡一切努力確保所有人、在所有地方、為所有人都有責任尊重人權，那麼宣布人權便是徒勞的」。[69] 在這些權利當中，首要的是生命權，從受孕之初直到自然終結，[70] 沒有生命權，便不可能行使任何其他權利。當這項基本權利遭到否認時——例如蓄意墮胎、殺害無辜者和安樂死的情況——我們所面對的，是教會認為極其嚴重的錯誤選擇。[71]
¶ 56
Looking at our own time, we cannot ignore the fact that the protection of human rights has been exposed to two particularly serious dangers. The first is that these rights are declared in a purely formal sense, while technological progress continues alongside covert or overt violations of human dignity. The second, which is in fact the root of the first, is the inability to recognize the foundation of their universality, since we have abandoned “the search for the solid foundations sustaining our decisions and our laws.” [72] Pope Francis urged us not to underestimate this last issue. He pointed out that when reason seriously examines human nature, it is capable of discovering values that apply to everyone, since they derive from human nature. If this task of inquiry were abandoned, it is conceivable that rights considered untouchable today might, in the future, end up being questioned or denied by those in power, perhaps after having obtained only an apparent consensus from populations that are frightened or manipulated. [73]
¶ 56
環顧我們自己的時代，我們不能忽略一個事實：人權的保障已暴露於兩個格外嚴重的危險之中。第一個危險是，這些權利僅以純粹形式上的方式被宣示，而技術進步卻伴隨著或明或暗地侵犯人性尊嚴的行為繼續前行。第二個危險——事實上是第一個危險的根源——即在於我們無法承認這些權利的普世性基礎，因為我們已放棄了「為支撐我們的決定和法律而尋求堅實基礎」的努力。[72] 教宗方濟各敦促我們不要低估這最後一個問題。他指出，當理性認真地審視人性時，它有能力發現那些適用於所有人的價值，因為這些價值源自人性本身。若這項探究的任務被放棄，那麼可以想見，那些今日被視為不可侵犯的權利，將來或許會遭到掌權者的質疑或否定，而在此之前，他們可能只是從受驚嚇或被操縱的民眾那裡取得了表面上的共識。[73]
¶ 57
Along with a greater awareness of the value of every human person and their rights, recognition of minority rights has also grown. Yet, there is still a long way to go to ensure that the rights of a great many, namely women, are equally and genuinely guaranteed throughout the world. It is a fact that “doubly poor are those women who endure situations of exclusion, mistreatment and violence, since they are frequently less able to defend their rights.” [74] It is, therefore, not enough to state simply that men and women have equal dignity and rights; it is necessary that this be reflected in concrete decisions, such as in laws, access to employment, education, social and political responsibilities, and the way society listens to and values women’s contributions. As long as this gap persists, we cannot say that society truly and fully recognizes that women have the same dignity as men.
¶ 57
隨著對每一個人及其權利的價值的意識有所增長，對少數群體權利的承認也有所增長。然而，要確保為數眾多的人——即女性——的權利能在全世界獲得平等而真實的保障，仍有漫漫長路。事實上，「那些身處排斥、虐待和暴力境遇的婦女，由於她們往往更難捍衛自己的權利，是雙重貧窮的人。」[74] 因此，僅僅宣稱男女享有同等的尊嚴與權利是不夠的；這必須體現在具體的決定中，例如法律、就業機會、教育、社會與政治責任，以及社會如何聆聽並重視婦女的貢獻。只要這個差距持續存在，我們就不能說社會真正且充分地承認婦女享有與男性同等的尊嚴。
¶ 58
It is individuals that matter, each and every person, together with their families. Social movements, communal ideologies and grand political proclamations in favor of a population are worthless unless they lead to the flourishing of persons — men and women — with their inalienable rights. Similarly, it is not enough to extol individual freedom or private enterprise if we then allow a multitude of people to continue living without decent work, protections or access to basic necessities.
¶ 58
重要的是每一個具體的人，每一個個體，以及他們的家庭。任何社會運動、集體意識形態，或為某個群體發出的堂皇政治宣言，若不能導致每一個人——男人和女人——連同其不可剝奪的權利得以茁壯成長，便毫無價值。同樣地，若我們一味頌揚個人自由或私營企業，卻任由無數的人繼續在沒有體面工作、缺乏保障或無法獲得基本生活所需的情況下過活，那也是不足夠的。
The principles of Social Doctrine
社會訓導的原則
The principle of the common good
公益原則
¶ 59
Recognizing that every man and woman possesses an inalienable dignity, together with rights that no human power can betray or nullify, requires us to shape the way we live together, including our economic and political choices, and the makeup of our cities. From this arises the first major principle of Social Doctrine that I wish to highlight: the common good. We can describe it as the social expression of the dignity recognized in every person. When Benedict XVI referred to the non-negotiable values that the Church must always defend, he included among them “the promotion of the common good.” [75] For a Christian, going beyond the narrow confines of one’s own interests and committing oneself, within the limits of one’s ability, to the common good is a non-negotiable value, as is the promotion of life.
¶ 59
承認每一個男人和女人都擁有不可剝奪的尊嚴，以及任何人間權力都無法出賣或廢除的權利，要求我們塑造我們共同生活的方式，包括我們的經濟和政治選擇，以及我們城市的構成。由此產生了我希望強調的教會社會訓導的第一個主要原則：公益。我們可以將其描述為在每一個人身上所承認的尊嚴的社會表達。當本篤十六世提到教會必須始終捍衛的那些不容妥協的價值時，他將「促進公益」[75] 包括在其中。為一個基督徒而言，超越自己利益的狹隘界限，並在自身能力範圍內投身於公益，正如促進生命一樣，是一項不容妥協的價值。
¶ 60
The Second Vatican Council affirmed that the common good consists in “the sum total of social conditions which allow people, either as groups or as individuals, to reach their fulfillment more fully and more easily.” [76] This definition provides us with a valuable initial reference point, because the common good cannot be reduced to a mere list of conditions or institutions. It is not the sum total of individual benefits, nor the intersection of their particular interests; it is a greater good that belongs to everyone, and it can only be achieved, nurtured and protected by our collective efforts. We can say that social action reaches its fullness when it is directed toward this shared good, just as a person’s moral action finds its fulfillment in the choice of the true good. [77]
¶ 60
梵蒂岡第二屆大公會議確認，公益在於「社會生活的條件總和，這些條件能讓社團及個別成員，更充分、更方便地達至自身的圓滿成全」[76]。這個定義為我們提供了一個寶貴的初始參照點，因為公益不能被簡化為僅僅是一系列條件或制度的清單。它不是個人利益的總和，也不是各人特殊利益的交集；它是一個屬於所有人的更大之善，而且只能透過我們的集體努力才能實現、培育和維護。我們可以說，當社會行動導向這共享之善時，便達至其圓滿，正如一個人的道德行動在於選擇真正的善時，才獲得其成全一樣。[77]
¶ 61
In this sense, we can say that the whole is “greater than the sum of its parts” [78] and that, for this very reason, “the mere sum of individual interests is not capable of generating a better world for the whole human family.” [79] Indeed, it is an illusion to think that simply pursuing one’s own progress without caring for others is sufficient for contributing to the good of all. This view ignores the inherent and specific value of the common good, which is the result of an “interdependence” [80] that creates a network of social good that expands and has an impact on people. The common good is a “plus,” the result of interaction and mutual influence that connects various actions, initiatives, efforts and decisions. If we were to add up the individual goods, we could not explain the existence of this “plus” that transcends them and, at the same time, enriches them.
¶ 61
就此而言，我們可以說，整體「大於其各部分之總和」[78]，而且正因如此，「僅僅將個別利益相加，並不能為整個人類大家庭帶來一個更美好的世界。」[79] 事實上，以為只需追求自身的進步而無需關顧他人，便足以促進所有人的福祉，這只是一個幻象。這種觀點忽視了公益本身固有而獨特的價值。公益乃是源於一種「相互依存」[80]的關係，這種關係交織成一張不斷擴展並影響眾人的社會善之網絡。公益是一個「更多的東西」，是各種行動、倡議、努力與抉擇彼此連結、相互影響而產生的結果。如果我們只是把個別的利益相加，便無法解釋這個超越它們、同時又使它們更形豐富的「更多的東西」的存在。
¶ 62
It is the pursuit of the common good that gives life to a people, understood not as a mere collection of individuals, but as a living reality in which people learn to recognize that they themselves are interconnected and jointly responsible for the res publica. In this sense, every person contributes to the building up of one’s people through “a slow and arduous effort calling for a desire for integration and a willingness to achieve this through the growth of a peaceful and multifaceted culture of encounter.” [81] Working together for the common good means having a shared vision. It is clear that there are many ideological and practical differences among people, as well as differing interests and frequent disagreements, but that does not mean it is impossible to engage in dialogue to establish a set of basic agreements that enable the creation of a shared vision, upon which everyone can move forward together.
¶ 62
正是對公益的追求賦予一個民族生命——這裡所理解的民族，不僅僅是個體的集合，而是一個活生生的現實，在其中人們學會認識到他們彼此相連，並為公共事務共同承擔責任。就此而言，每一個人都透過「一項緩慢而艱巨的努力，這要求一種融合的渴望，以及透過一種和平而多元的相遇文化的成長來實現這一切的意願」[81]，為自己民族的建設作出貢獻。為公益而共同努力，意味著擁有一個共同的願景。顯然，人們之間存在著許多意識形態和實踐上的差異，以及不同的利益和頻繁的分歧，但這並不意味著不可能展開對話，以建立一套基本共識，從而能夠創造一個共同的願景，使眾人都能在此基礎上攜手前行。
¶ 63
It is the State’s responsibility to ensure cohesion, unity and the proper organization of civil society, so that the common good can be pursued with everyone’s contribution. In practical terms, this means that public authorities have the delicate duty to “harmonize the different sectoral interests with the requirements of justice,” [82] seeking a balance between individual interests and the common good, without leaving behind the most vulnerable. When politics abandons a long-term perspective and reduces itself to short-term calculations or sterile polarizations, then the language of the common good loses credibility, and, at the same time, social inequalities and divisions grow.
¶ 63
國家有責任確保公民社會的凝聚力、合一及妥善組織，使公益能在每個人的貢獻下得以實現。具體而言，這意味著公共當局肩負一項精細的職責，即「按正義的要求，協調各種行業利益」[82]，在個人利益與公益之間尋求平衡，不遺棄最脆弱的人。當政治放棄長遠視野，淪為短視的計算或徒然的兩極對立時，公益的語言便失去可信性，而與此同時，社會的不平等與分裂也隨之加劇。
¶ 64
This also applies to international politics. As the divide between nations widens, a mentality of confrontation and aggression begins to take hold, and the difficult path toward a more united and fraternal world suffers new and painful setbacks. In this context, speaking of a shared journey toward a more just development for the entire human family “sounds like madness.” [83] Yet we must not lose hope. I invite everyone to conceive of ways of cooperating and of more effective international institutions, capable of safeguarding the global common good without compromising the legitimate diversity of peoples and nations. Indeed, the promotion of the common good can never be separated from respect for the right of peoples to exist, to preserve their own identity and to contribute their unique qualities to the family of nations. [84] Moreover, any attempt or plan to eliminate or subjugate a nation is gravely immoral and therefore unacceptable.
¶ 64
這也適用於國際政治。隨著各國之間的鴻溝日益擴大，對抗與侵略的心態開始扎根，走向一個更加團結友愛的世界這條艱難道路，亦遭受了新的痛苦挫折。在此背景下，談論人類大家庭共同邁向更公正發展的歷程，「聽起來就像瘋話」。[83] 然而，我們絕不能失去希望。我邀請所有人構思合作的方式，並建立更有效的國際機構，使其能夠在維護各民族與國家合法多元性的同時，保障全球公益。事實上，促進公益永遠不能與尊重各民族生存的權利、保存自身身分的權利，以及為萬民大家庭貢獻其獨特稟賦的權利分割開來。[84] 再者，任何企圖或計劃消滅或征服一個民族的行為，都是嚴重不道德的，因此絕不可接受。
The principle of the universal destination of goods
財富普世用途原則
¶ 65
“Among the numerous implications of the common good, immediate significance is taken on by the principle of the universal destination of goods.” [85] First of all, this principle reminds us that the earth’s goods — soil, water, air and natural resources — are given by God to the entire human family to sustain the lives of all, and that every person has an inherent right to the use of such goods, both now and in the future. Saint John Paul II recalled that, “God gave the earth to the whole human race for the sustenance of all its members, without excluding or favoring anyone.” [86] Consequently, “it is not in accordance with God’s plan to use this gift in such a way that its benefits accrue solely to a select few.” [87] Today, we are called to recognize that this universal destination applies not only to material goods, but also to immaterial and cultural goods.
¶ 65
「在公益的眾多含義中，財貨的普遍歸向原則具有直接的意義。」[85] 首先，這項原則提醒我們，大地的財貨——土壤、水源、空氣和自然資源——是天主賜予整個人類大家庭，用以維持所有人生命的，每一個人無論是現在還是將來，都擁有使用這些財貨的固有權利。聖若望保祿二世曾提醒說：「天主將大地賜給整個人類，是為維持其所有成員的生活，不排除也不偏待任何人。」[86] 因此，「若以這樣的方式利用這份恩賜，使其利益僅歸於少數人，這並不符合天主的計劃。」[87] 今天，我們蒙召認識到，這種普遍歸向不僅適用於物質財貨，也適用於非物質和文化財貨。
¶ 66
Certainly there is a right to private property, which has its own specific meaning and purpose, yet it is always subordinate to the universal destination of goods. According to John Paul II, this subordination is the golden rule of social conduct and the “first principle of the whole ethical and social order.” [88] In the Church’s tradition, property has been viewed as a means of protecting and managing goods so that they may better serve the common good. Since “the Christian tradition has never recognized the right to private property as absolute or inviolable,” [89] its social function must not be considered a mere theological opinion, but a doctrine of the Church, already present in Sacred Scripture and in the writings of the Church Fathers. For this reason, Pope Francis reminded us that solidarity, when lived out in its fullest sense, also means “to restore to the poor what belongs to them.” [90]
¶ 66
無疑，私有產權是存在的，且有其特定的意義與目的，然而它始終從屬於財貨的普遍歸宿。若望保祿二世指出，這種從屬關係是社會行為的黃金規律，也是「整個倫理與社會秩序的首要原則」。[88] 在教會的傳統中，財產向來被視為一種保護和管理財貨的工具，使之能更好地服務於公益。既然「基督信仰傳統從未承認私有產權是絕對或不可侵犯的」[89]，那麼其社會功能便不應被視為單純的神學見解，而是一項教會的教義，早已存在於聖經及教會聖師的著作中。為此，教宗方濟各提醒我們，當團結關懷以最圓滿的意義生活出來時，也意味著「將屬於窮人的歸還給他們」。[90]
¶ 67
Today, among the goods that are universally intended for everyone, we must also include new forms of property, such as patents, algorithms, digital platforms, technological infrastructure and data. In a context where the wealth of nations depends increasingly on knowledge and technology, when these goods remain concentrated in the hands of a few, without adequate forms of sharing and access, a new imbalance is created that contradicts the universal destination of goods. In turn, it widens the gap between the included and the excluded, between those who can participate in the digital revolution and those who remain on the margins. Furthermore, care for our common home and our responsibility toward the poor and future generations require that the use of the goods of creation and the new possibilities offered by technology be regulated in such a way as to respect the environment, avoid waste and prevent new forms of exploitation.
¶ 67
今日，在那些普遍為所有人而設的財物之中，我們也必須將新形式的財產納入其中，例如專利、演算法、數碼平台、技術基礎設施和數據。在國家的財富日益依賴知識與技術的背景下，當這些財物仍然集中在少數人手中，而沒有適當的分享和獲取途徑時，就會產生一種新的失衡，違背了財物的普遍歸屬。這反過來又擴大了被包容者與被排斥者之間、能夠參與數碼革命者與仍處於邊緣者之間的鴻溝。此外，對我們共同家園的關懷，以及我們對窮人和未來世代所肩負的責任，要求我們在使用受造界的財物及技術所提供的新可能性時，必須以尊重環境、避免浪費並防止新形式的剝削的方式加以規範。
The principle of subsidiarity
輔助原則
¶ 68
The principle of subsidiarity stems from the very same understanding of the human person that has guided our reflection on dignity and the common good. If every woman and man is called to take ownership of his or her own life and to contribute to the formation of society, then social institutions must also respect and support this responsibility. The Social Doctrine of the Church refers to subsidiarity as the principle according to which the role of individuals, families, local communities and intermediary organizations should not be supplanted by higher-level authorities. Moreover, higher-level institutions must recognize, protect and promote the freedom and creativity of lower-level entities, coordinating their contributions so that they can cooperate effectively for the common good. [91]
¶ 68
輔助性原則源自對人的同一種理解——正是這種理解引導了我們對尊嚴與公益的反思。倘若每一個男女都蒙召去掌管自己的生命，並為社會的塑造作出貢獻，那麼社會制度也必須尊重並支持這份責任。教會社會訓導將輔助性原則界定為：個人、家庭、地方團體及中間組織的角色，不應被更高層級的權力當局所取代。不僅如此，更高層級的機構必須承認、保護和促進較低層級實體的自由與創造力，協調它們的貢獻，使之能有效地為公益而合作。[91]
¶ 69
Starting with Leo XIII and the beginnings of modern social teaching, the Church has insisted that neither the individual nor the family should be subsumed by the State, but should be allowed to act freely, as far as possible, without harming the common good. [92] Saint John Paul II took up and developed this perspective, noting that the political community is at the service of civil society and that the State must protect the common good, intervening when necessary, but without permanently supplanting the responsibilities of intermediary organizations and social institutions. [93] Subsidiarity does not justify the State’s disengagement, but rather guides its actions. Indeed, public intervention is necessary precisely to enable all social actors to fulfill their mission without being stifled. It is the responsibility of the political community to create the conditions that allow individuals, families, associations and intermediary organizations to fulfil their mission in society, without being replaced or reduced to mere facilitators. [94]
¶ 69
從良十三世及現代社會訓導的萌芽時期開始，教會便堅持，個人或家庭都不應被國家所吞沒，而應在盡可能不損害公益的前提下，獲准自由地行事。[92] 聖若望保祿二世接納並發展了這一觀點，指出政治團體是為公民社會服務的，而國家必須保護公益，在必要時進行干預，但不得永久性地取代中介組織和社會機構的責任。[93] 輔助原則並不為國家的撤離提供理據，反而引導其行動。事實上，公共干預之所以必要，正是為了使所有社會行動者都能履行其使命，而不受壓制。政治團體有責任創造條件，讓個人、家庭、社團及中介組織能夠在社會中履行其使命，而不被取代或淪為純粹的促進者。[94]
¶ 70
This principle encourages us to move beyond any form of paternalistic or welfare-based management of societal life, but instead to promote a culture of shared responsibility in a State that values citizens’ initiative, and a civil society capable of forging bonds and mobilizing energies in the service of the common good. In accordance with the principle of subsidiarity, decisions are made at the closest level possible to the persons involved, thereby fostering community life and avoiding people being presented with decisions that have already been taken. In this way people can participate in the decision-making process. When families, associations, local communities, volunteer organizations and those in the so-called “third sector” are recognized and supported, social life becomes more accessible to people, services become more attuned to real needs, and solutions are more creative and respectful of the dignity of each person. [95]
¶ 70
這項原則鼓勵我們超越任何形式以家長式管理或福利為本的社會生活管理模式，轉而推動一種共同承擔責任的文化，在一個重視公民主動性的國家，以及一個能夠建立聯繫、動員力量以服務公益的公民社會中實現。按照輔助性原則，決策應在盡量接近當事人的層面上作出，從而促進團體生活，避免人們面對已事先決定的方案。如此一來，人們便能參與決策過程。當家庭、社團、地方社群、義工組織以及所謂「第三界別」的機構得到認可和支持時，社會生活就會變得更貼近人民，服務亦會更切合實際需要，而解決方案則會更具創意，並且更尊重每一個人的尊嚴。[95]
¶ 71
The principle of subsidiarity applies especially in the context of the digital revolution. Here, the highest level is not the State, but rather major economic and technological actors that exercise de facto power over the conditions of everyday life. This level, which monopolizes expertise, data and decision-making authority, involves companies and platforms that define conditions for access, rules of visibility, forms of interaction, and even economic opportunities. The principle of subsidiarity requires that such processes not be imposed from above in an opaque and unilateral manner, but instead be directed toward the common good with transparency, accountability and meaningful forms of participation (including independent checks, transparency regarding algorithms, equitable access to data and avenues for recourse). [96]
¶ 71
輔助性原則尤其在數碼革命的脈絡中適用。在這裡，最高的層級並非國家，而是那些對日常生活狀況行使實際權力的大型經濟和科技行動者。這一層級壟斷了專業知識、數據和決策權力，涉及那些界定准入條件、可見度規則、互動形式，乃至經濟機會的公司和平台。輔助性原則要求，這類過程不得以不透明和單方面的方式自上而下強加於人，反而必須以透明度、問責制及有意義的參與形式（包括獨立檢查、演算法的透明度、公平的數據取用及申訴途徑）為指引，邁向公益。[96]
¶ 72
In this context, States and transnational institutions are called to ensure fair rules and effective safeguards, so that local communities, intermediary organizations, schools, universities, religious institutions and associations have a voice and can contribute to the discernment of choices that affect people’s daily lives, such as employment, access to services, data management and digital environments. When it comes to decisions regarding economic flows and digital platforms, as well as the governance of data and algorithms, we cannot allow a handful of actors to dictate these processes on their own; instead, we must build forms of cooperation that respect the various levels of the global community and make them jointly responsible for the common good. [97]
¶ 72
在此背景下，各國和跨國機構蒙召制定公平的規則和有效的保障措施，使地方社群、中介組織、學校、大學、宗教機構和社團能夠發聲，並能夠協助分辨那些影響人民日常生活的選擇，例如就業、獲取服務的機會、數據管理和數碼環境。在關乎經濟流動和數碼平台的決策，以及數據和演算法的治理方面，我們不能讓少數參與者獨自支配這些過程；相反，我們必須建立各種合作形式，既尊重全球社群的不同層面，又使他們共同為公益承擔責任。[97]
The principle of solidarity
團結原則
¶ 73
Having considered the common good and subsidiarity, I would like to reflect on the principle of solidarity. This emerges from a vision of the human person generated by faith, namely that every human being is created in the image of God and is part of a network of relationships that bind him or her to others, to specific populations and to creation. Saint Paul VI observed that the obligations of solidarity, justice and charity are rooted in the human and supernatural fraternal bonds that unite individuals and populations. [98] Fraternity is not merely an aspiration of believers, but is a social and political reality to be embodied in communal choices and endeavors. Solidarity, then, is the concrete recognition that the future of each individual is connected to the future of all; indeed, “no one is saved alone.” [99] The close link between subsidiarity and solidarity thereby becomes evident. It is thus clear that there is an intimate link between subsidiarity and solidarity. When subsidiarity is not linked to solidarity, it ends up becoming merely the protection of particular interests; when solidarity is not supported by subsidiarity, it degenerates into a form of welfare that does not foster responsibility. [100] This interconnectedness also pertains to the responsibility of authentic participation. Solidarity is expressed when each person, both individually and collectively, takes part in the life of the community — by staying informed, engaging with others, making their voice heard and contributing to public decisions and choices — while also assuming real responsibility so that the common good is achieved through shared decision-making.
¶ 73
在思考過公益和輔助性原則之後，我願反思團結關懷的原則。這原則是從信仰所孕育的人觀中產生出來的，即每一個人都是按天主的肖像所造，並置身於一個關係網絡中，將他或她與他人、與特定的民族及與受造界聯繫在一起。聖保祿六世指出，團結關懷、正義和愛德的義務，植根於將個人和民族聯合在一起的人性與超性的兄弟情誼。[98] 兄弟情誼不僅是信友的願景，更是一個社會和政治的現實，必須體現在共同體的抉擇和努力中。因此，團結關懷就是具體地認識到，每一個人的未來都與所有人的未來息息相關；事實上，「沒有人能獨自得救。」[99] 輔助性原則與團結關懷之間的密切聯繫由此變得顯而易見。因此很清楚，輔助性原則與團結關懷之間存在著內在的聯繫。當輔助性原則不與團結關懷相連時，它最終只會成為對特殊利益的維護；而當團結關懷得不到輔助性原則的支持時，它便會退化為一種無法培養責任感的福利形式。[100] 這種相互關聯性也關係到真正參與的責任。當每一個人，無論是個人還是集體，都參與到團體生活中——透過了解情況、與他人互動、表達意見，並為公共決策和選擇作出貢獻——同時承擔起真正的責任，好使公益能透過共同的決策得以實現時，團結關懷便得以體現。
¶ 74
In many areas, we are already experiencing a kind of “ de facto solidarity,” for our lives are intertwined; digital networks connect people and communities across the world in real time, and global economies and communications mean that events in one place have a far-reaching impact. This network of relationships, however, only constitutes solidarity in the fullest sense of the word when it becomes a conscious choice. Faith invites us to see this reality as a call: we are not merely neighbors to one another, but entrusted to each other, so that each of us may take responsibility, as best we can, for the lives and wounds of our brothers and sisters. Solidarity arises precisely when we decide not to remain indifferent to what happens to our neighbor but instead to transform unavoidable bonds — economic, cultural and technological — into paths of sharing, cooperation and mutual care, embracing the idea of “thinking and acting in terms of community.” [101]
¶ 74
在許多領域中，我們已然體會到某種「事實上的休戚與共」，因為我們的生命交織相連；數碼網絡將世界各地的人與群體實時連結起來，而全球經濟與通訊更意味著，一個地方發生的事件會產生深遠的影響。然而，這張關係網唯有在成為一項有意識的抉擇時，才構成最完整意義上的休戚與共。信仰邀請我們將這現實視為一項召叫：我們不僅彼此為鄰，更被彼此交託，好使我們每個人都能盡己所能，為我們弟兄姊妹的生命與創傷承擔責任。休戚與共的真正產生，恰恰在於我們決意不再對近人身上所發生的事無動於衷，而是將那些無可避免的聯繫——經濟的、文化的和技術的——轉化為分享、合作與互相關懷的道路，擁抱「以團體的角度思考和行動」的理念。[101]
¶ 75
The Church’s social teaching emphasizes that solidarity is both a principle and a virtue. As a principle, it expresses the objective order of relationships among individuals, groups and peoples, pointing to an awareness of interdependence whereby the good of each person depends on the good of others. As a virtue, it requires a “firm and persevering determination” [102] to strive for the common good, with particular attention to those most in need. Pope Francis noted that solidarity is “a way of making history” [103] that creates communities and not just masses of individuals. For this reason, it requires a modest and shared way of life, the ability to forego immediate benefits in order to create opportunities for others in the future, and a willingness to challenge habits and privileges — including those related to digital consumption and the use of technology — when they prevent others from living with dignity.
¶ 75
教會的社會訓導強調，團結關懷既是一項原則，也是一種德行。作為原則，它表達了個人、群體和民族之間關係的客觀秩序，指向一種對相互依存的自覺——每個人的福祉取決於他人的福祉。作為德行，它要求一種「堅定而持久的決心」[102] 去為公益奮鬥，並特別關顧那些最有需要的人。教宗方濟各指出，團結關懷是「一種造就歷史的方式」[103]，它創造的是真正的團體，而不只是個體的群眾。為此緣故，它要求一種簡樸而共享的生活方式，具備捨棄當下利益以在未來為他人締造機會的能力，並願意挑戰那些妨礙他人有尊嚴地生活的習慣和特權——包括與數碼消費及科技使用相關的習慣和特權。
¶ 76
In a world marked by increasingly close connections between people, communities and nations, solidarity also takes on a global dimension. Benedict XVI strongly emphasized the link between development, justice and responsibility toward future generations, stating that authentic development requires solidarity and inter-generational justice, [104] as well as an awareness of the bonds that unite us to the natural environment. Today, this responsibility also extends to digital and information infrastructure. Like the natural environment, the “digital ecosystem” can be preserved or exploited, shared or monopolized. Solidarity demands that decisions regarding data, algorithms, platforms and artificial intelligence take into account not only the immediate benefit for a few, but also the impact on all peoples and on future generations.
¶ 76
在人與人、團體與團體、國與國之間的聯繫日益緊密的世界中，團結關懷亦具有全球性的幅度。本篤十六世極力強調發展、正義與對後代責任之間的連繫，申明真正的發展要求團結關懷與代際正義，[104] 以及對我們與自然環境之間聯繫的意識。今天，這份責任也延伸至數碼和資訊基礎設施。如同自然環境一樣，「數碼生態系統」可以被保存，也可以被剝削；可以被分享，也可以被壟斷。團結關懷要求，在作出有關數據、演算法、平台和人工智能的決定時，不僅要考慮少數人的當下利益，更要考慮對所有民族及後代子孫的影響。
The principle of social justice
社會正義原則
¶ 77
For the Christian community, social justice is a concrete way of following Jesus and remaining faithful to the Gospel. In the New Testament, Jesus proclaims the “good news to the poor” ( Lk 4:18) and identifies himself with the lowly, the sick, the imprisoned and strangers (cf. Mt 25:31-46). He thus teaches us that justice is born from, and fulfilled in, fraternity, because the way we approach and relate to the least among us becomes, in concrete terms, the measure of our relationship with God and with our brothers and sisters. Justice, however, concerns not only the behavior of individuals, but also the way in which the structures of society are conceived and organized. In this regard, the Second Vatican Council reminds us that every institution is called to serve the human person and his or her dignity. [105] Social justice is, therefore, characterized by the capacity of a social, economic and political order to allow everyone — particularly the weakest — to live a truly dignified life, without leaving anyone behind.
¶ 77
對基督信仰團體而言，社會正義是跟隨耶穌、忠於福音的一條具體道路。在新約中，耶穌向「貧窮人宣告喜訊」（路 4:18），並將自己與卑微的人、患病的人、被囚禁的人和異鄉人視為同一（參瑪 25:31-46）。祂藉此教導我們：正義生於弟兄情誼，並在弟兄情誼中得以圓滿，因為我們走近並對待我們中最弱小者的方式，具體而言，就成了我們與天主、以及與我們弟兄姊妹關係的尺度。然而，正義不僅關乎個人的行為，也關乎社會結構被構思和組織的方式。就此而言，梵蒂岡第二屆大公會議提醒我們，每一個制度都蒙召為人及其尊嚴服務。[105] 因此，社會正義的特徵，在於一種社會、經濟和政治秩序能夠使每一個人——尤其是最弱小者——度一個真正有尊嚴的生活，不讓任何人被遺棄。
¶ 78
The recent Magisterium has insisted that social justice begins with the least among us.
